# Active Runs Ledger

Coordination surface for CLIs (Claude Code agents, manual sessions, skill
invocations) operating concurrently on this checkout. Each session that
materially edits the working tree should touch this file twice:

1. **At session start (Phase 0):** read this file, scan `## Active` for
   running entries. If any entry's declared paths overlap with this
   session's planned scope AND the entry is less than 2 hours old AND its
   status is `started`, surface the conflict to the user before proceeding
   (options: abort, coordinate, or proceed-with-awareness). Then append
   your own entry under `## Active`.
2. **At session end (Phase 11/13):** move your `## Active` entry to the
   top of `## Recently completed`, update its status to `completed (commit:
   <sha>)` or `aborted (<reason>)`. Trim entries older than 14 days from
   `## Recently completed`.

If your session crashes, your entry stays under `## Active` with a stale
timestamp — the next session can recognize it as abandoned.

## Conventions

- Timestamps are local time, format `YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM`.
- `Paths` declares the directories or globs the session expects to read or
  write. Be specific enough that overlap is meaningful (`src/features/agents/sub_chat/`
  is good; `src/` is too broad to be useful).
- The `## Active` section is the source of truth; `## Recently completed`
  is a rolling history window.
- Concurrent edits to this file: re-read on Edit failure, repeat the
  conflict check, retry. The Edit tool's unique-old-string rule prevents
  silent clobbers.

- **[2026-05-24 — started] fix(home): cockpit live-refresh on Athena compose + header backdrop-blur flicker**
  - **Source:** User-reported. (1) Cockpit empty-state→Athena flow: chat works but cockpit doesn't populate per Athena message (stale until forced re-render); after Athena answers the chat should auto-shrink so the composed content is visible; shrunk chat 30px thinner.   - **Paths:** `src/features/home/sub_cockpit/CockpitPanel.tsx` (subscribe to `COMPANION_COMPOSE_COCKPIT_EVENT` → refetch + clear contextual), `src/features/plugins/companion/CompanionPanel.tsx` (compact width 380→350px), `src/features/personas/PersonasPage.tsx` (flicker fix — see below). ContentLayout.tsx + ContentHeaderSkeleton.tsx were touched then REVERTED (back to original min-w-[80vw], no diff). Surgical, frontend-only, on master.
  - **Status:** in progress — tsc clean, eslint 0 on touched files. Chat width 350px confirmed OK by user.
    - FLICKER ROOT CAUSE (corrected): NOT the ContentHeader. It's the app-wide background **grid layer** at `PersonasPage.tsx:271` — a full-screen `absolute inset-0` CSS `repeating-linear-gradient` of 1px blue lines (32px cells) behind all content (`z-10`). The layer isn't GPU-isolated, so it shares a paint layer with hover-repainting content; every pointer-move re-rasterizes the gradient, and at fractional Windows DPI a 1px line maps to non-integer device px → shimmer, worst at top/right edges. Fix: `transform-gpu backface-hidden` on the grid + fade layers → one-time raster, composite-only thereafter. Earlier `min-w-[80vw]`→`w-full` guess was WRONG (only narrowed the header) and was reverted.
  - **Branch:** master
  - **Note:** Path-disjoint from active sessions (overview-batch=overview/home-widgets, density=globals.css/themeStore, athena-tour=onboarding). transform-gpu is a light 2D layer promotion, unlike the backdrop-blur previously removed from this same block for the ARM64 compositor freeze. Awaiting user HMR confirmation; fallbacks if it persists: pre-rasterized SVG data-URI grid, or edge-mask to drop the top/right boundary lines.

- **[2026-05-24 — completed (commits: 7bb31ca6d, merge 8710dcfff)] idea-330cd93f — self-scaling RelativeTime primitive with shared ticker**
  - **Source:** Idea requirement (ui_perfectionist). Dozens of relative-time labels each spun their own `setInterval` (PeerList 15s, RelativeTime 15s, rotation ticker 60s), wasting wake-ups, drifting out of sync, and showing stale labels up to 15s past a boundary.
  - **Shipped:** New `src/hooks/utility/timing/relativeTimeTicker.ts` — a single app-wide ticker. `useRelativeTimeTick(ts)` derives cadence from a label's age (1s sub-minute, 30s sub-hour, 5m beyond); `useFixedTicker(ms)` subscribes at a constant cadence. The ticker runs at the finest cadence any live subscriber needs and re-renders all of them on one tick (auto-stops when empty). Migrated: `RelativeTime` primitive (was local 15s interval — every `<RelativeTime>` app-wide now benefits), `PeerList` (dropped ad-hoc `useRelativeTime` hook), `ExecutionListRow` mobile card (static `formatRelativeTime()` → live `<RelativeTime>`), `useRotationTicker` (credential countdown now coalesces onto the shared ticker). 12 new unit tests.

- **[2026-05-14 12:30 → 13:15] ort-arm64-fix — predev cache-override for pyke's mislabeled aarch64 tarball**
  - **Status:** completed (commit `93073a8c2` on master).
  - **Source:** in-session user request after `npm run tauri:dev` failed on arm64 Snapdragon X Elite (X1E78100) with `lld-link: error: machine type x64 conflicts with arm64` for `libort_sys-ddea945a6dca0f73.rlib`. `clean:ort` was tried first and did not help — the next download produced the same broken bytes, because the SHA256 in `ort-sys-2.0.0-rc.9/dist.txt` is the hash of the mislabeled tarball itself, not of what should be inside.
  - **Root cause:** `ort-sys 2.0.0-rc.9` dist.txt line 8 maps `aarch64-pc-windows-msvc` to `parcel.pyke.io/.../ortrs_static-v1.20.0-aarch64-pc-windows-msvc.tgz` SHA256 `C09BFF5582BCA2EC583E49A32E7B1B406AC930CB18791C3165E82B53516C27DE`. The tarball is named arm64 and hashes correctly; `dumpbin /HEADERS` of the extracted `onnxruntime.lib` reports `8664 machine (x64)`. Confirmed upstream defect, not stale cache. `fastembed 4.9.1` pins both `ort = "=2.0.0-rc.9"` and `ort-sys = "=2.0.0-rc.9"`, so escape via version bump requires a major dep upgrade (fastembed 5.x + ort rc.12) with API risk and no guarantee the upstream is fixed.
  - **Paths shipped (commit `93073a8c2`):**
    - `scripts/ensure-ort-cache.mjs` (NEW, ~416 lines) — sniffs cached `onnxruntime.lib`'s actual COFF machine field, downloads Microsoft's official ORT 1.20.0 from `github.com/microsoft/onnxruntime/releases/download/v1.20.0/onnxruntime-win-<arch>-1.20.0.zip` and places it into pyke's expected cache slot when the cache is missing/wrong; tracks state via `.personas-ort-fix-applied` sentinel; evicts stale `libort_sys-*.rlib` from `target/<profile>/deps/` when it predates the sentinel (mtime comparison) so cargo's incremental compile rebuilds it.
    - `package.json` — added `ensure:ort-cache` alias + `pretauri:dev` / `pretauri:dev:stable` / `pretauri:dev:test:full` / `pretauri:build` / `pretauri:build:stable` lifecycle hooks. Lite variants skipped (don't compile `ml`).
    - `.claude/CLAUDE.md` — added "Picking dev variants — when to use lite vs full" decision table and "When builds get slow or break" recovery section.
    - `docs/development/build.md` — replaced obsolete "Known issue: ort + Windows ARM64" workaround list (lite / cross-compile / wait-for-stable) with the auto-fix description, including verification steps and a note about the STATIC→DYNAMIC linkage trade-off.
  - **Linkage change:** switches ORT from STATIC (pyke's 290 MB onnxruntime.lib bundled into the exe) to DYNAMIC (Microsoft's small import lib + 12 MB `onnxruntime.dll`). The `ort` crate's `copy-dylibs` default feature places the DLL next to the exe in dev and release builds; tauri-bundler picks it up from `target/release/` for installers.
  - **Validation:** `npm run tauri:dev` (canonical, `desktop-full`) completes end-to-end on aarch64. Logs show `Embedding model AllMiniLML6V2Q loaded successfully`, `mDNS service registered`, `Frontend time-to-interactive: 12848.5 ms`, and the embedding doctrine ingest from `companion::brain::doctrine` runs. The `cpuinfo: Unknown chip model 'Snapdragon X Elite'` warning is from upstream `cpuinfo` and is informational only (not a build error).
  - **Headline:** First reliable fix for the `ort-sys 2.0.0-rc.9` mislabeled-tarball bug on arm64 Windows hosts — replaces three workarounds (use lite / cross-compile to x64 / wait for ort 2.0 stable) with a self-healing predev fix that survives `clean:ort`. CI is unaffected (x64 runners, pyke's x64 tarball is correct; the fix is a no-op there). Build-process review identified follow-ups: auto-killing orphan Vite on port 1420, expanding `check-build-cache.mjs` to validate cached binary architecture (currently only checks rustc host-triple drift), and chaining `ensure:ort-cache` after `clean:ort` so the operation always leaves the system in a known-good state.

- **[2026-05-12 14:00 → 15:10] i18n-dead-keys — warn-only scanner + 11-section deletion sweep**
  - **Status:** completed (commits `633a38125` scanner, `d193a5588` deletion on master).
  - **Phase 1 — scanner (`633a38125`):** `scripts/i18n/find-unused-i18n-keys.mjs` (NEW, ~310 lines), `package.json` (added `check:i18n-dead` script).
  - **Approach:** prefix-match scanner. Reuses `flattenKeys()` shape from `check-coverage.mjs`. Walks `src/**/*.{ts,tsx}` (skips `i18n/`, `__tests__`, `*.test.*`, `*.spec.*`, `generated/`); re-includes 4 sanctioned shape adapters (`useReleasesTranslation`, `useSidebarTranslation`, `useTranslatedError`, `tokenMaps`). Captures `t.<dotted.path>` via regex, plus `tokenLabel(t, '<category>', …)` → `status_tokens.<category>` umbrella, plus `ERROR_KEY_MAP` `keyPrefix:` values parsed out of `useTranslatedError.ts` → `error_registry.<prefix>_{message,suggestion}`. Any en.json key whose path matches or is a prefix of a captured reference is "used". Modes: default (warn, exit 0), `--strict` (exit 1), `--json`, `--full`, `--ignore-prefix=a,b`.
  - **First-run result:** 2152 / 11867 keys flagged unused (18.1%). Worst-offender sections — `overview` 531, `agents` 529, `vault` 256, `plugins` 133. Fully-dead sections (100% unused, strong signal): `toasts` 58/58, `composition` 47/47, `prompt_lab` 46/46, `error_explanation` 42/42, `tests` 27/27, `drift_labels` 26/26, `alerts` 15/15, `deploy_errors` 13/13, `command_palette` 11/11, `validation` 9/9, `teams` 6/6, `protocol_labels` 4/4, `cli` 2/2, `auth` 1/1. Spot-grepped `t.toasts`, `t.composition`, `t.prompt_lab`, `t.alerts`, `t.error_explanation`, `t.cli`, `t.auth` → zero matches in `src/`, confirming the scanner is not generating false positives on whole-section dead-letter cases.
  - **Phase 2 — deletion sweep (`d193a5588`):** Removed 11 fully-dead top-level sections from all 14 locale files + `routeSections.ts` + regenerated `generated/types.ts` and `generated/enSectionStrings.ts` + dropped 143 deleted `section-locales/<lang>/*.json` files. Sections: `toasts, composition, prompt_lab, error_explanation, tests, drift_labels, command_palette, validation, teams, protocol_labels, cli`. Net: 278 keys removed, 160 files changed, 8697 lines deleted. **Did NOT delete** `alerts, deploy_errors, auth` despite scanner flagging them 100% unused — tsc verification caught real references through the `import { en }` Proxy shim in 3 Zustand slices (`authStore`, `alertSlice`, `deployTarget`); restored them from HEAD before commit.
  - **Verification:** `npx tsc --noEmit` clean on deletion-commit state (7 pre-existing errors in `PersonaSettingsTab.tsx` are unrelated icon-picker WIP from a concurrent session). `node scripts/i18n/check-coverage.mjs`: 0 extras across all 14 locales (symmetric deletion held); 318 missing per locale is pre-existing translation lag (warn-only). Re-run of dead-key scanner: 2152 → 1874 unused (16.2%, down from 18.1%).
  - **Parallel-safety discipline applied:** working tree had 6 in-flight i18n keys from at least 2 other concurrent sessions (3 in `overview.messages_view.*` driving `MessageDetailModal.tsx` changes, 3 in `shared.forms_extra.*` driving icon-picker work in `PersonaSettingsTab.tsx`). Constructed clean commit state via "HEAD - 11 sections" approach (no user edits in staged content), committed, then restored the 6 in-flight keys back to working-tree en.json + regenerated types.ts/enSectionStrings.ts so the other sessions could continue uninterrupted. Zero `git stash` use; explicit `git add <path>` per file across both commits; `git diff --cached --stat` verification matched intent (3 files in scanner commit, 160 in deletion commit).
  - **Scanner false-positive finding:** the `import { en }` Proxy shim from `src/i18n/en.ts` is used at module-scope in Zustand slices and helpers (per CLAUDE.md back-compat shim section, ~48 modules). The static scanner doesn't see `en.<section>.<key>` patterns — only `t.<section>.<key>`. Discovered the gap by running `npx tsc --noEmit` after the first deletion attempt (3 sections came back with errors). Known follow-up: extend the scanner's reference-capture regex to also match `\ben\.([a-z_][\w.]*)`. Until then, scanner output should be cross-checked with tsc on a regen'd type tree before any deletion.
  - **Headline:** 278 unreferenced i18n keys (2.3% of catalog) deleted across 11 fully-dead top-level sections — every one a fossil from a retired migration (simple-mode, prompt_lab, command_palette, etc.). The "delete then run tsc as the post-commit hook" workflow the user suggested caught the 3 false-positive sections cleanly before they shipped. Remaining 1874 unused keys (16.2%) are scattered sub-key dead spots inside active sections — much harder to clean (each needs a manual look); awaiting follow-up plan on whether to triage manually, extend the scanner to detect `en.X.Y` and `getRegistryString` patterns to shrink the false-positive surface, or wire as a non-blocking warn step in pre-push.

A future slice plumbs `connector_strategy::resolve_auth_token` for transparent refresh; the indirection cost is one extra Mutex hop on every Teams delivery so the 401-and-re-auth path is the right shipping default. (c) Per-destination "needs setup" surfaces during build (amber chip + warning hint + attach-button label) but doesn't block launch — empty config falls back to credential's `scoped_resources` at delivery time via Slice 1's `merged_channel_config`. If both are empty, Slice 1's actionable error fires on the first message attempt — the user sees a precise pointer rather than silent drop. (d) Hydration only honours the parent prop on initial mount via a lazy `useState` initializer — once the user starts editing, parent re-renders can't clobber in-flight changes. (e) `JsonValue` cast at the picker's `setConfigValue` write site is structural — runtime objects from picker inputs are valid `JsonValue` instances, the cast just nudges TS through the optional-vs-required value variance. **Pre-existing-bug catches:** none.

  - **Source:** in-session conversation; user request to add open-source TTS as alternative to ElevenLabs.
